<li id="cite_note-75"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-75">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Dijkstra, Edsger W (1982). <a class="external text" href="http://www.cs.utexas.edu/users/EWD/transcriptions/EWD04xx/EWD447.html" rel="nofollow">"On the role of scientific thought"</a>. <i>Selected writings on Computing: A Personal Perspective</i>. New York, NY, USA: Springer-Verlag. pp. 60–66. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-387-90652-5" title="Special:BookSources/0-387-90652-5">0-387-90652-5</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEdsger+W.+Dijkstra&amp;rft.atitle=On+the+role+of+scientific+thought&amp;rft.aufirst=Edsger+W&amp;rft.aulast=Dijkstra&amp;rft.btitle=Selected+writings+on+Computing%3A+A+Personal+Perspective&amp;rft.date=1982&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.cs.utexas.edu%2Fusers%2FEWD%2Ftranscriptions%2FEWD04xx%2FEWD447.html&amp;rft.isbn=0-387-90652-5&amp;rft.pages=60-66&amp;rft.place=New+York%2C+NY%2C+USA&amp;rft.pub=Springer-Verlag&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-76"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-76">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Brown, Kyle; Craig, Gary; Hester, Greg (2003). <i>Enterprise Java Programming with IBM WebSphere</i>, 2nd Edition (IBM Press), p. 5. "Most experienced IT professionals will agree that developing and adhering to a standard architecture is key to the success of large-scale <a href="/wiki/Software_development" title="Software development">software development</a>. Computer pioneer Edsger Dijkstra validated this notion when he developed <i><a href="/wiki/THE_multiprogramming_system" title="THE multiprogramming system">THE</a></i> operating system in 1968. Since then, layered architectures have proved their viability in technological domains, such as hardware and networking.<br/>
Layering has proved itself in the operating system domain; however, the same benefits are available when applied to e-commerce or to thin client–oriented applications. Layered architectures have become essential in supporting the iterative development process by promoting reusability, scalability, and maintainability."</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-77"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-77">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Grier, David Alan. <a class="external text" href="https://www.computer.org/web/closer-than-you-might-think/layers-upon-layers" rel="nofollow">"<i>Closer Than You Might Think: Layers upon Layers</i>"</a>. IEEE Computer Society<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">12 August</span> 2015</span>. <q>We generally trace the idea of building computer systems in layers back to a 1967 paper that the Dutch computer scientist Edsger Dijkstra gave to a joint IEEE Computer Society/ACM conference. Prior to this paper, engineers had struggled with the problem of how to organize software. If you look at early examples of programs, and you can find many in the electronic library of the Computer Society, you will find that most code of that era is complicated, difficult to read, hard to modify, and challenging to reuse. In his 1967 paper, Dijkstra described how software could be constructed in layers and gave an example of a simple operating system that used five layers. He admitted that this system might not be a realistic test of his ideas but he argued that the "larger the project, the more essential the structuring!"<br/>
The idea of using layers to control complexity has become a mainstay of software architecture. We see it in many forms and apply it to many problems. We see it in the hierarchy of classes in object-oriented programming and in the structure of Service-Oriented Architecture.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEdsger+W.+Dijkstra&amp;rft.au=Grier%2C+David+Alan&amp;rft.btitle=Closer+Than+You+Might+Think%3A+Layers+upon+Layers&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.computer.org%2Fweb%2Fcloser-than-you-might-think%2Flayers-upon-layers&amp;rft.pub=IEEE+Computer+Society&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-78"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-78">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Albin, Stephen T. (Wiley Publishing, Inc., 2003), p. 3</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-79"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-79">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Dijkstra, Edsger W. <i>Over seinpalen (EWD-74)</i>. E.W. Dijkstra Archive. Center for American History, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_at_Austin" title="University of Texas at Austin">University of Texas at Austin</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEdsger+W.+Dijkstra&amp;rft.aufirst=Edsger+W&amp;rft.aulast=Dijkstra&amp;rft.btitle=Over+seinpalen+%28EWD-74%29&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.pub=Center+for+American+History%2C+University+of+Texas+at+Austin&amp;rft.series=E.W.+Dijkstra+Archive&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span> (<a class="external text" href="http://www.cs.utexas.edu/users/EWD/ewd00xx/EWD74.PDF" rel="nofollow">original</a>; <a class="external text" href="http://www.cs.utexas.edu/users/EWD/transcriptions/EWD00xx/EWD74.html" rel="nofollow">transcription</a>)</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-80"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-80">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Per_Brinch_Hansen" title="Per Brinch Hansen">Brinch Hansen, Per</a> (2002). <i>The Origin of Concurrent Programming: From Semaphores to Remote Procedure Calls</i>. (Springer)., p. 8</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-81"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-81">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">McCormick, John W.; Singhoff, Frank; Hugues, Jérôme (2011). <i>Building Parallel, Embedded, and Real-Time Applications with Ada</i> (Cambridge University Press), p. 5. "The notion of the concurrent program as a means for writing parallel programs without regard for the underlying hardware was first introduced by Edsger Dijkstra (1968). Moti Ben-Ari (1982) elegantly summed up Dijkstra's idea in three sentences: 'Concurrent programming is the name given to programming notation and techniques for expressing potential parallelism and solving the resulting synchronization and communication problems. Implementation of parallelism is a topic in computer systems (hardware and software) that is essentially independent of concurrent programming. Concurrent programming is important because it provides an abstract setting in which to study parallelism without getting bogged down in the implementation details.<span style="padding-right:.2em;">'</span>"</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-82"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-82">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Anderson, J.H.; Kim, Y.-J.; Herman, T. (2003). <i>Shared-Memory Mutual Exclusion: Major Research Trends Since 1986</i>. (Distributed Computing 16(2-3), 75-110)</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-83"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-83">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Alagarsamy, K. (2003). <i>Some Myths About Famous Mutual Exclusion Algorithms</i>. (ACM SIGACT News, 34(3): 94-103)</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-84"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-84">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Raynal, Michel (2013). <i>Concurrent Programming: Algorithms, Principles, and Foundations</i> (Springer), p. vi. "Since the early work of E.W. Dijkstra (1965), who introduced the mutual exclusion problem, the concept of a process, the semaphore object, the notion of a weakest precondition, and guarded commands (among many other contributions), synchronization is no longer a catalog of tricks but a domain of computing science with its own concepts, mechanisms, and techniques whose results can be applied in many domains. This means that process synchronization has to be a major topic of any computer science curriculum."</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-85"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-85">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">James, Mike (1 May 2013). <a class="external text" href="http://www.i-programmer.info/history/people/144-dijkstra.html?start=1" rel="nofollow">"<i>Edsger Dijkstra - The Poetry of Programming</i>"</a>. i-programmer.info<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">12 August</span> 2015</span>. <q>Although Dijkstra will always be remembered for structured programming, and for his style and approach, he also invented many other of the standard ideas of programming. If you are struggling with multi-threaded programming you may have encountered the semaphore, and the idea of the "deadly embrace". These, and more, are the result of Dijkstra's work on concurrent programming. He showed how this particularly difficult area of programming could be made relatively safe.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEdsger+W.+Dijkstra&amp;rft.au=James%2C+Mike&amp;rft.btitle=Edsger+Dijkstra+-+The+Poetry+of+Programming&amp;rft.date=2013-05-01&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.i-programmer.info%2Fhistory%2Fpeople%2F144-dijkstra.html%3Fstart%3D1&amp;rft.pub=i-programmer.info&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-86"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-86">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Hoare, C. A. R. (2004). <a class="external text" href="http://www.usingcsp.com/cspbook.pdf" rel="nofollow">"Communicating Sequential Processes"</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(PDF)</span>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.usingcsp.com/" rel="nofollow">usingcsp.com</a> (originally published in 1985 by Prentice Hall International).</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEdsger+W.+Dijkstra&amp;rft.aufirst=C.+A.+R.&amp;rft.aulast=Hoare&amp;rft.btitle=Communicating+Sequential+Processes&amp;rft.date=2004&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.usingcsp.com%2Fcspbook.pdf&amp;rft.pub=%5Bhttp%3A%2F%2Fwww.usingcsp.com%2F+usingcsp.com%5D+%28originally+published+in+1985+by+Prentice+Hall+International%29&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span> <span class="error citation-comment" style="font-size:100%">External link in <code style="color:inherit; border:inherit; padding:inherit;">|publisher=</code> (<a href="/wiki/Help:CS1_errors#param_has_ext_link" title="Help:CS1 errors">help</a>)</span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-87"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-87">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Shasha, Dennis; Lazere, Cathy (1998). <i>Out of Their Minds: The Lives and Discoveries of 15 Great Computer Scientists</i>. (Copernicus), p. 64</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-88">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="external text" href="http://www.podc.org/dijkstra" rel="nofollow">Edsger W. Dijkstra Prize in Distributed Computing (ACM Symposium on Principles of Distributed Computing)</a>. The citation for the prize reads: "The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edsger_W._Dijkstra_Prize_in_Distributed_Computing" title="Edsger W. Dijkstra Prize in Distributed Computing">Edsger W. Dijkstra Prize in Distributed Computing</a> is named for Edsger Wybe Dijkstra (1930–2002), a pioneer in the area of distributed computing. His foundational work on concurrency primitives (such as the semaphore), concurrency problems (such as mutual exclusion and deadlock), reasoning about concurrent systems, and self-stabilization comprises one of the most important supports upon which the field of distributed computing is built. No other individual has had a larger influence on research in principles of distributed computing."</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-89"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-89">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="external text" href="http://www.eatcs.org/index.php/dijkstra-prize" rel="nofollow">Edsger W. <li id="cite_note-95"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-95">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Back, Ralph-Johan; Wright, Joakim (1998), p. v</span></li>
